       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/%C3%81vila_(province)" title="Ávila (province)">
        Ávila
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Salamanca" title="Salamanca">
        Salamanca
       </a>
       . Once he had secured the Borders, King Alfonso conquered the powerful
       <a href="/wiki/Taifa_of_Toledo" title="Taifa of Toledo">
        Taifa kingdom of Toledo
       </a>
       in 1085.
       <a href="/wiki/Toledo,_Spain" title="Toledo, Spain">
        Toledo
       </a>
       , which was the former capital of the Visigoths, was a very important landmark, and the conquest made Alfonso renowned throughout the Christian world. However, this "conquest" was conducted rather gradually, and mostly peacefully, during the course of several decades. It was not until after sporadic and consistent population resettlements had taken place that Toledo was decisively conquered.
      </p>
      <p>
       Alfonso VI was first and foremost a tactful monarch who chose to understand the kings of taifa and employed unprecedented diplomatic measures to attain political feats before considering the use of force. He adopted the title
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Imperator_totius_Hispaniae" title="Imperator totius Hispaniae">
         Imperator totius Hispaniae
        </a>
       </i>
       ("Emperor of all
       <a href="/wiki/Hispania" title="Hispania">
        Hispania
       </a>
       ", referring to all the Christian kingdoms of the Iberian Peninsula, and not just the modern country of Spain). Alfonso's more aggressive policy towards the taifas worried the rulers of those kingdoms, who called on the African
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Almoravid" title="Almoravid">
        Almoravids
       </a>
       for help.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id="Kingdom_of_Navarre_.28824.E2.80.931620.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Kingdom_of_Navarre_(824–1620)">
        Kingdom of Navarre (824–1620)
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Reconquista&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Kingdom of Navarre (824–1620)">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Navarre" title="Kingdom of Navarre">
        Kingdom of Navarre
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Pamplona" title="Kingdom of Pamplona">
        Kingdom of Pamplona
       </a>
       primarily extended along either side of the Pyrenees on the Atlantic Ocean. The kingdom was formed when local leader Íñigo Arista led a revolt against the regional Frankish authority and was elected or declared King in Pamplona (traditionally in 824), establishing a kingdom inextricably linked at this stage to their kinsmen, the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Muwallad" title="Muwallad">
        muwallad
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Banu_Qasi" title="Banu Qasi">
        Banu Qasi
       </a>
       of Tudela.
      </p>
      <p>
       Although relatively weak until the early 11th century, Pamplona took a more active role after the accession of
       <a href="/wiki/Sancho_III_of_Pamplona" title="Sancho III of Pamplona">
        Sancho the Great
       </a>
       (1004–1035). The kingdom expanded greatly under his reign, as it absorbed Castile, Leon, and what was to be Aragon, in addition to other small counties that would unite and become the Principality of Catalonia. This expansion also led to the independence of Galicia, as well as gaining overlordship over
       <a href="/wiki/Gascony" title="Gascony">
        Gascony
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       In the 12th century, however, the kingdom contracted to its core, and in 1162 King
       <a href="/wiki/Sancho_VI_of_Navarre" title="Sancho VI of Navarre">
        Sancho VI
       </a>
       declared himself
       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Navarre" title="Kingdom of Navarre">
        king of Navarre
       </a>
       . Throughout its early history, the Navarrese kingdom engaged in frequent skirmishes with the Carolingian Empire, from which it maintained its independence, a key feature of its history until 1513.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id="Kingdom_of_Aragon_.281035.E2.80.931706.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Kingdom_of_Aragon_(1035–1706)">
        Kingdom of Aragon (1035–1706)
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Reconquista&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Kingdom of Aragon (1035–1706)">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Aragon" title="Kingdom of Aragon">
        Kingdom of Aragon
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jaume_I,_Cantigas_de_Santa_Maria,_s.XIII.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="649" data-file-width="697" height="205" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Jaume_I%2C_Cantigas_de_Santa_Maria%2C_s.XIII.jpg/220px-Jaume_I%2C_Cantigas_de_Santa_Maria%2C_s.XIII.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Jaume_I%2C_Cantigas_de_Santa_Maria%2C_s.XIII.jpg/330px-Jaume_I%2C_Cantigas_de_Santa_Maria%2C_s.XIII.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Jaume_I%2C_Cantigas_de_Santa_Maria%2C_s.XIII.jpg/440px-Jaume_I%2C_Cantigas_de_Santa_Maria%2C_s.XIII.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Jaume_I,_Cantigas_de_Santa_Maria,_s.XIII.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The Moors request permission from
         <a href="/wiki/James_I_of_Aragon" title="James I of Aragon">
          James I of Aragon
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The Kingdom of Aragon was an offshoot of the Kingdom of Navarre. It was formed when
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sancho_III_of_Navarre" title="Sancho III of Navarre">
        Sancho III of Navarre
       </a>
       decided to divide his large realm among all his sons. Aragon was the portion of the realm which passed to
       <a href="/wiki/Ramiro_I_of_Aragon" title="Ramiro I of Aragon">
        Ramiro I of Aragon
       </a>
       , an illegitimate son of Sancho III. The kingdoms of Aragon and Navarre were several times united in personal union until the death of
       <a href="/wiki/Alfonso_the_Battler" title="Alfonso the Battler">
        Alfonso the Battler
       </a>
       in 1135.
      </p>
      <p>
       The Kingdom of Aragon collected a number of territories in the Mediterranean, known as the
       <a href="/wiki/Crown_of_Aragon" title="Crown of Aragon">
        Crown of Aragon
       </a>
       .
       <a href="/wiki/James_I_of_Aragon" title="James I of Aragon">
        James I of Aragon
       </a>
       , also known as James the Conqueror, expanded Aragon to the north, south and east. James also signed the
       <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Corbeil_(1258)" title="Treaty of Corbeil (1258)">
        Treaty of Corbeil (1258)
       </a>
       , which released him from the nominal suzerainty of the King of France.
      </p>
      <p>
       Early in his reign, James attempted to reunite the Aragonese and Navarrese crowns through a treaty with the childless
       <a href="/wiki/Sancho_VII_of_Navarre" title="Sancho VII of Navarre">
        Sancho VII of Navarre
       </a>
       . But the Navarrese nobles rejected him, and chose the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Theobald_IV_of_Champagne" title="Theobald IV of Champagne">
        Theobald IV of Champagne
       </a>
       in his stead. It was his distant descendant,
       <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_II_of_Aragon" title="Ferdinand II of Aragon">
        Ferdinand II of Aragon
       </a>
       , who brought Aragon to the height of its power through the conquest of Upper Navarre (Navarre south of the Pyrenees) and Granada.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id="Kingdom_of_Portugal_.281139.E2.80.931910.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Kingdom_of_Portugal_(1139–1910)">
        Kingdom of Portugal (1139–1910)
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Reconquista&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Kingdom of Portugal (1139–1910)">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Portugal" title="Kingdom of Portugal">
        Kingdom of Portugal
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:GeraldoGeraldesSemPavor.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="365" height="247" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/GeraldoGeraldesSemPavor.jpg/180px-GeraldoGeraldesSemPavor.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/GeraldoGeraldesSemPavor.jpg/270px-GeraldoGeraldesSemPavor.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/GeraldoGeraldesSemPavor.jpg/360px-GeraldoGeraldesSemPavor.jpg 2x" width="180"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:GeraldoGeraldesSemPavor.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Statue of
         <a href="/wiki/Gerald_the_Fearless" title="Gerald the Fearless">
          Gerald the Fearless
         </a>
         . A Portuguese folk hero with the head of a Moor
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In 1139, after an overwhelming victory in the
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Ourique" title="Battle of Ourique">
        Battle of Ourique
       </a>
       against the
       <a href="/wiki/Almoravid_dynasty" title="Almoravid dynasty">
        Almoravids
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Afonso_Henriques" title="Afonso Henriques">
        Afonso Henriques
       </a>
       was proclaimed the first
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_Portuguese_monarchs" title="List of Portuguese monarchs">
        King of Portugal
       </a>
       by his troops. According to the legend, Christ announced from heaven
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2017)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       Afonso's great deeds, whereby he would establish the first
       <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Cortes" title="Portuguese Cortes">
        Portuguese Cortes
       </a>
       at
       <a href="/wiki/Lamego" title="Lamego">
        Lamego
       </a>
       and be crowned by the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Archbishop_of_Braga" title="Archbishop of Braga">
        Archbishop of Braga
       </a>
       . In the
       <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Zamora" title="Treaty of Zamora">
        Treaty of Zamora
       </a>
       in 1143,
       <a href="/wiki/Alfonso_VII_of_Le%C3%B3n_and_Castile" title="Alfonso VII of León and Castile">
        Alfonso VII of León and Castile
       </a>
       recognized Portuguese independence from the Kingdom of León.
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1147, Portugal
       <a href="/wiki/Conquest_of_Santar%C3%A9m" title="Conquest of Santarém">
        captured Santarém
       </a>
       , and seven months later the city of
       <a href="/wiki/Lisbon" title="Lisbon">
        Lisbon
       </a>
       was also brought under Portuguese control after the
       <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Lisbon" title="Siege of Lisbon">
        Siege of Lisbon
       </a>
       . By the papal bull
       <a href="/wiki/Manifestis_Probatum" title="Manifestis Probatum">
        Manifestis Probatum
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Pope_Alexander_III" title="Pope Alexander III">
        Pope Alexander III
       </a>
       recognized Afonso Henriques as King of Portugal in 1179.
      </p>
      <p>
       With
       <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">
        Portugal
       </a>
       finally recognized as an independent kingdom by its neighbours,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Afonso_Henriques" title="Afonso Henriques">
        Afonso Henriques
       </a>
       and his successors, aided by
       <a href="/wiki/Crusades" title="Crusades">
        Crusaders
       </a>
       and the military monastic orders the
       <a href="/wiki/Knights_Templar" title="Knights Templar">
        Knights Templar
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Order_of_Aviz" title="Order of Aviz">
        Order of Aviz
       </a>
       or the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Order_of_Saint_James_of_the_Sword" title="Order of Saint James of the Sword">
        Order of Saint James
       </a>
       , pushed the
       <a href="/wiki/Moors" title="Moors">
        Moors
       </a>
       to the
       <a href="/wiki/Algarve" title="Algarve">
        Algarve
       </a>
       on the southern coast of Portugal. After several campaigns, the Portuguese part in the
       <i>
        Reconquista
       </i>
       came to an end with the definitive capture of the Algarve in 1249. With all of Portugal now under the control of
       <a href="/wiki/Afonso_III_of_Portugal" title="Afonso III of Portugal">
        Afonso III of Portugal
       </a>
       , religious, cultural and ethnic groups became gradually homogenized.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:OrderOfCristCross.svg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="512" data-file-width="512" height="180" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/OrderOfCristCross.svg/180px-OrderOfCristCross.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/OrderOfCristCross.svg/270px-OrderOfCristCross.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/OrderOfCristCross.svg/360px-OrderOfCristCross.svg.png 2x" width="180"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:OrderOfCristCross.svg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Cross of the
         <a href="/wiki/Order_of_Christ_(Portugal)" title="Order of Christ (Portugal)">
          Order of Christ
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       After the completion of the
       <i>
        Reconquista
       </i>
       , the Portuguese territory was a Roman Catholic realm. Nonetheless,
       <a href="/wiki/Denis_of_Portugal" title="Denis of Portugal">
        Denis of Portugal
       </a>
       carried out a short war with
       <a href="/wiki/Crown_of_Castile" title="Crown of Castile">
        Castile
       </a>
       for possession of the towns of
       <a href="/wiki/Serpa" title="Serpa">
        Serpa
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moura_Municipality" title="Moura Municipality">
        Moura
       </a>
       . After this, Denis avoided war; he signed the Treaty of Alcanizes with
       <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_IV_of_Castile" title="Ferdinand IV of Castile">
        Ferdinand IV of Castile
       </a>
       in 1297, establishing the present-day borders.
      </p>
      <p>
       During the suppression of the Knights Templar all over
       <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">
        Europe
       </a>
       , under the influence of
       <a href="/wiki/Philip_IV_of_France" title="Philip IV of France">
        Philip IV of France
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Pope_Clement_V" title="Pope Clement V">
        Pope Clement V
       </a>
       requesting its annihilation by 1312, King Denis reinstituted the Templars of
       <a href="/wiki/Tomar" title="Tomar">
        Tomar
       </a>
       as the
       <a href="/wiki/Order_of_Christ_(Portugal)" title="Order of Christ (Portugal)">
        Order of Christ
       </a>
       in 1319. Denis believed that the Order's assets should by their nature stay in any given Order instead of being taken by the King, largely for the Templars' contribution to the
       <i>
        Reconquista
       </i>
       and the reconstruction of Portugal after the wars.
      </p>
      <p>
       The experience gained during the battles of the
       <i>
        Reconquista
       </i>
       was fundamental to
       <a href="/wiki/Conquest_of_Ceuta" title="Conquest of Ceuta">
        Conquest of Ceuta
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2017)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       the first step to the establishment of the
       <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Empire" title="Portuguese Empire">
        Portuguese Empire
       </a>
       . Likewise, the contact with
       <a href="/wiki/Islamic_Golden_Age" title="Islamic Golden Age">
        Muslim's navigation techniques and sciences
       </a>
       enabled the creation of
       <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Renaissance" title="Portuguese Renaissance">
        Portuguese nautical innovations
       </a>
       such as the
       <a href="/wiki/Caravel" title="Caravel">
        Caravel
       </a>
       - the principal Portuguese ship during their voyages of exploration in the
       <a href="/wiki/Age_of_Discovery" title="Age of Discovery">
        Age of Discovery
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">
        <a href="#cite_note-32">
         [31]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Christian_infighting">
        Christian infighting
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Reconquista&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Christian infighting">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       Clashes and raids on bordering Andalusian lands did not keep the Christian kingdoms from battling among themselves or allying with Muslim kings. Some Muslim kings had Christian-born wives or mothers. Some Christian champions, like
       <a href="/wiki/El_Cid" title="El Cid">
        El Cid
       </a>
       , were contracted by
       <a href="/wiki/Taifa" title="Taifa">
        taifa
       </a>
       kings to fight against their neighbours. Indeed,
       <a href="/wiki/El_Cid" title="El Cid">
        El Cid
       </a>
       's first battle experience was gained fighting for a Muslim state against a Christian state. At the
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Graus" title="Battle of Graus">
        Battle of Graus
       </a>
       in 1063, he and other Castilians fought on the side of
       <a href="/wiki/Ahmad_al-Muqtadir" title="Ahmad al-Muqtadir">
        al-Muqtadir
       </a>
       , Muslim
       <a href="/wiki/Sultan" title="Sultan">
        sultan
       </a>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/Zaragoza" title="Zaragoza">
        Zaragoza
       </a>
       , against the forces of
       <a href="/wiki/Ramiro_I_of_Aragon" title="Ramiro I of Aragon">
        Ramiro I of Aragon
       </a>
       . There is even an instance of a Crusade being declared against another Christian king in Iberia.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JosephCallaghan_33-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-JosephCallaghan-33">
         [32]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Following the disastrous defeat of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alfonso_VIII" title="Alfonso VIII">
        Alfonso VIII
       </a>
       , King of Castile, at
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Alarcos" title="Battle of Alarcos">
        Alarcos
       </a>
       , Kings
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alfonso_IX" title="Alfonso IX">
        Alfonso IX
       </a>
       of León and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sancho_VII" title="Sancho VII">
        Sancho VII
       </a>
       of Navarre entered an alliance with the
       <a href="/wiki/Almohad_Caliphate" title="Almohad Caliphate">
        Almohads
       </a>
       and invaded Castile in 1196. By the end of the year Sancho VII had dropped out of the war under Papal pressure. Early in 1197, at the request of
       <a href="/wiki/Sancho_I_of_Portugal" title="Sancho I of Portugal">
        Sancho I
       </a>
       , King of Portugal, Pope
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Celestine_III" title="Celestine III">
        Celestine III
       </a>
       declared a Crusade against Alfonso IX and released his subjects from their responsibilities to the king, declaring that "the men of his realm shall be absolved from their fidelity and his dominion by authority of the apostolic see."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JosephCallaghan_33-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-JosephCallaghan-33">
         [32]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Together the Kings of Portugal, Castile, and
       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Aragon" title="Kingdom of Aragon">
        Aragon
       </a>
       invaded León. In the face of this onslaught combined with pressure from the Pope, Alfonso IX was finally forced to sue for peace in October 1197.
      </p>
      <p>
       In the late years of
       <i>
        Al-Andalus
       </i>
       , Castile had the might to conquer the remains of the kingdom of
       <a href="/wiki/Granada" title="Granada">
        Granada
       </a>
       , but the kings preferred to claim the tribute of the Muslim
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Parias" title="Parias">
         parias
        </a>
       </i>
       . The trade of Granadan goods and the parias were a major means by which African gold entered
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Medieval_Europe" title="Medieval Europe">
        medieval Europe
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Christian_repopulation_of_Iberian_Peninsula">
        Christian repopulation of Iberian Peninsula
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Reconquista&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Christian repopulation of Iberian Peninsula">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Further information:
       <a href="/wiki/Medieval_demography" title="Medieval demography">
        Medieval demography
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Repoblaci%C3%B3n" title="Repoblación">
        Repoblación
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The
       <i>
        Reconquista
       </i>
       was a process not only of war and conquest, but also of
       <a href="/wiki/Colonization" title="Colonization">
        repopulation
       </a>
       . Christian kings moved their own people to locations abandoned by Muslims in order to have a population capable of defending the borders. The main repopulation areas were the
       <a href="/wiki/Douro" title="Douro">
        Douro
       </a>
       Basin (the northern plateau), the high
       <a href="/wiki/Ebro" title="Ebro">
        Ebro
       </a>
       valley (
       <a href="/wiki/La_Rioja_(Spain)" title="La Rioja (Spain)">
        La Rioja
       </a>
       ) and central
       <a href="/wiki/Catalonia" title="Catalonia">
        Catalonia
       </a>
       . The repopulation of the
       <a href="/wiki/Douro" title="Douro">
        Douro
       </a>
       Basin took place in two distinct phases. North of the river, between the 9th and 10th centuries, the "pressure" (or
       <i>
        presura
       </i>
       ) system was employed. South of the
       <a href="/wiki/Douro" title="Douro">
        Douro
       </a>
       , in the 10th and 11th centuries, the
       <i>
        presura
       </i>
       led to the "charters" (
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Foral" title="Foral">
         forais
        </a>
       </i>
       or
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fueros" title="Fueros">
         fueros
        </a>
       </i>
       ).
       <i>
        Fueros
       </i>
       were used even south of the Central Range.
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <i>
        presura
       </i>
       referred to a group of peasants who crossed the mountains and settled in the abandoned lands of the Douro Basin. Asturian laws promoted this system, for instance granting a peasant all the land he was able to work and defend as his own property. Of course, Asturian and Galician minor nobles and clergymen sent their own expeditions with the peasants they maintained. This led to very feudalised areas, such as
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Le%C3%B3n_(province)" title="León (province)">
        León
       </a>
       and Portugal, whereas Castile, an arid land with vast plains and harsh climate, only attracted peasants with no hope in Biscay. As a consequence, Castile was governed by a single count, but had a largely non-feudal territory with many
       <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/freeman" title="wikt:freeman">
        free
       </a>
       peasants.
       <i>
        Presuras
       </i>
       also appear in Catalonia, when the count of Barcelona ordered the Bishop of Urgell and the count of Gerona to repopulate the plains of
       <a href="/wiki/Vic" title="Vic">
        Vic
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       During the 10th century and onwards, cities and towns gained more importance and power, as commerce reappeared and the population kept growing.
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Fuero" title="Fuero">
         Fueros
        </a>
       </i>
       were
       <a href="/wiki/Charter" title="Charter">
        charters
       </a>
       documenting the privileges and usages given to all the people repopulating a town. The
       <i>
        fueros
       </i>
       provided a means of escape from the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Feudal_system" title="Feudal system">
        feudal system
       </a>
       , as
       <i>
        fueros
       </i>
       were only granted by the monarch. As a result, the town council was dependent on the monarch alone and, in turn, was required to provide
       <i>
        auxilium
       </i>
       – aid or troops – for their monarch. The military force of the towns became the
       <i>
        caballeros villanos
       </i>
       . The first
       <i>
        fuero
       </i>
       was given by count
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fern%C3%A1n_Gonz%C3%A1lez" title="Fernán González">
        Fernán González
       </a>
       to the inhabitants of
       <a href="/wiki/Castrojeriz" title="Castrojeriz">
        Castrojeriz
       </a>
       in the 940's. The most important towns of medieval Iberia had
       <i>
        fueros
       </i>
       , or
       <i>
        forais
       </i>
       . In Navarre,
       <i>
        fueros
       </i>
       were the main repopulating system. Later on, in the 12th century, Aragon also employed the system; for example, the
       <i>
        fuero
       </i>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/Teruel" title="Teruel">
        Teruel
       </a>
       , which was one of the last fueros, in the early 13th century.
      </p>
      <p>
       From the mid-13th century on, no more charters were granted, as the demographic pressure had disappeared and other means of re-population were created.
       <i>
        Fueros
       </i>
       remained as city charters until the 18th century in Aragon, Valencia and Catalonia and until the 19th century in Castile and Navarre.
       <i>
        Fueros
       </i>
       had an immense importance for those living under them, who were prepared to go to war to defend their rights under the charter. In the 19th century, the abolition of the
       <i>
        fueros
       </i>
       in Navarre would be one of the causes of the
       <a href="/wiki/Carlist_Wars" title="Carlist Wars">
        Carlist Wars
       </a>
       . In Castile, disputes over the system contributed to the war against Charles I (
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Castilian_War_of_the_Communities" title="Castilian War of the Communities">
        Castilian War of the Communities
       </a>
       ).
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Muslim_decline_and_defeat">
        Muslim decline and defeat
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Reconquista&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Muslim decline and defeat">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Fall_of_the_Caliphate">
        Fall of the Caliphate
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Reconquista&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Fall of the Caliphate">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Batalla_del_Puig_por_Marzal_de_Sas_(1410-20).jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1407" data-file-width="1000" height="310" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Batalla_del_Puig_por_Marzal_de_Sas_%281410-20%29.jpg/220px-Batalla_del_Puig_por_Marzal_de_Sas_%281410-20%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Batalla_del_Puig_por_Marzal_de_Sas_%281410-20%29.jpg/330px-Batalla_del_Puig_por_Marzal_de_Sas_%281410-20%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Batalla_del_Puig_por_Marzal_de_Sas_%281410-20%29.jpg/440px-Batalla_del_Puig_por_Marzal_de_Sas_%281410-20%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Batalla_del_Puig_por_Marzal_de_Sas_(1410-20).jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The
         <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Puig" title="Battle of the Puig">
          Battle of the Puig
         </a>
         at
         <a href="/wiki/El_Puig" title="El Puig">
          El Puig de Santa Maria
         </a>
         in 1237
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       During the 9th century the Berbers returned to Africa in the aftermath of revolts. Many governors of large cities distant from the capital, Córdoba, had planned to establish their independence. Then, in 929, the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Emir_of_C%C3%B3rdoba" title="Emir of Córdoba">
        Emir of Córdoba
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Abd-ar-Rahman_III" title="Abd-ar-Rahman III">
        Abd-ar-Rahman III
       </a>
       ), the leader of the Umayyad dynasty, declared himself
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Caliph" title="Caliph">
        Caliph
       </a>
       , independent from the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Abbasid" title="Abbasid">
        Abbasids
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Baghdad" title="Baghdad">
        Baghdad
       </a>
       . He took all the military, religious, and political power and reorganised the army and the bureaucracy.
      </p>
      <p>
       After regaining control over the dissident governors, Abd-ar-Rahman III tried to conquer the remaining Christian kingdoms of the Iberian peninsula, attacking them several times and forcing them back beyond the Cantabrian mountains. Abd-ar-Rahman's grandson later became a puppet in the hands of the great
       <a href="/wiki/Vizier" title="Vizier">
        Vizier
       </a>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Al-Mansur_Ibn_Abi_Aamir" title="Al-Mansur Ibn Abi Aamir">
        Almanzor
       </a>
       (
       <i>
        al-Mansur
       </i>
       , "the victorious"). Almanzor waged several campaigns attacking and sacking Burgos, León, Pamplona, Barcelona, and
       <a href="/wiki/Santiago_de_Compostela" title="Santiago de Compostela">
        Santiago de Compostela
       </a>
       before his death in 1002.
      </p>
      <p>
       Between Almanzor's death and 1031, Al-Andalus suffered many civil wars, which ended in the division into the
       <a href="/wiki/Taifa" title="Taifa">
        Taifa kingdoms
       </a>
       . The taifas were small kingdoms, established by the city governors. The result was many (up to 34) small kingdoms, each centered upon its capital. Their governors had no larger-scale vision of the Moorish presence in the Iberian peninsula and had no qualms about attacking their neighbouring kingdoms whenever they could gain advantage by doing so.
      </p>
      <p>
       The split into the taifa states weakened the Islamic presence, and the Christian kingdoms further advanced as Alfonso VI conquered Toledo in 1085. Surrounded by their enemies, taifa rulers sent a desperate appeal to the Berber chieftain
       <a href="/wiki/Yusuf_ibn_Tashfin" title="Yusuf ibn Tashfin">
        Yusuf ibn Tashfin
       </a>
       , leader of the Almoravids.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2016)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Almoravids">
        Almoravids
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Reconquista&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Almoravids">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Almoravid_dynasty" title="Almoravid dynasty">
        Almoravid dynasty
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Almoravid" title="Almoravid">
        Almoravids
       </a>
       were a Muslim militia primarily composed of Berber and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ethnic_groups_of_Africa" title="Ethnic groups of Africa">
        African
       </a>
       Moors, and unlike previous Muslim rulers, they were not so tolerant towards Christians and Jews. Their armies entered the Iberian peninsula on several occasions (1086, 1088, 1093) and defeated King Alfonso at the
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Sagrajas" title="Battle of Sagrajas">
        Battle of Sagrajas
       </a>
       in 1086, but initially their purpose was to unite all the taifas into a single Almoravid Caliphate. Their actions halted the southward expansion of the Christian kingdoms. Their only defeat came at
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Valencia_(city_in_Spain)" title="Valencia (city in Spain)">
        Valencia
       </a>
       in 1094, due to the actions of
       <a href="/wiki/El_Cid" title="El Cid">
        El Cid
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Meanwhile, Navarre lost all importance under King
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sancho_IV_of_Navarre" title="Sancho IV of Navarre">
        Sancho IV
       </a>
       , for he lost Rioja to
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sancho_II_of_Castile" title="Sancho II of Castile">
        Sancho II of Castile
       </a>
       , and nearly became the vassal of Aragon. At his death, the Navarrese chose as their king
       <a href="/wiki/Sancho_Ram%C3%ADrez" title="Sancho Ramírez">
        Sancho Ramírez
       </a>
       , King of Aragon, who thus became Sancho V of Navarre and I of Aragon. Sancho Ramírez gained international recognition for Aragon, uniting it with Navarre and expanding the borders south, conquering
       <i>
        Wasqa
        <sup>
         t
        </sup>
       </i>
       <a href="/wiki/Huesca" title="Huesca">
        Huesca
       </a>
       deep in the valleys in 1096 and building a fort, El Castellar, 25 km from
       <i>
        Saraqusta
        <sup>
         t
        </sup>
       </i>
       <a href="/wiki/Zaragoza" title="Zaragoza">
        Zaragoza
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Catalonia came under intense pressure from the taifas of Zaragoza and
       <a href="/wiki/Taifa_of_L%C3%A9rida" title="Taifa of Lérida">
        Lérida
       </a>
       , as well as from internal disputes, as Barcelona suffered a dynastic crisis that led to open war among the smaller counties. But by the 1080s, the situation had calmed down, and the dominion of Barcelona over the smaller counties was restored.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Almohads">
        Almohads
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Reconquista&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Almohads">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Almohad_dynasty" title="Almohad dynasty">
        Almohad dynasty
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mapa_reconquista_almohades-en.svg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="368" data-file-width="474" height="171" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Mapa_reconquista_almohades-en.svg/220px-Mapa_reconquista_almohades-en.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Mapa_reconquista_almohades-en.svg/330px-Mapa_reconquista_almohades-en.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Mapa_reconquista_almohades-en.svg/440px-Mapa_reconquista_almohades-en.svg.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mapa_reconquista_almohades-en.svg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Extent of the
         <i>
          Reconquista
         </i>
         into Almohad territory as of 1157.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       After a brief period of disintegration (the second
       <a href="/wiki/Taifa" title="Taifa">
        Taifa
       </a>
       period), the Almohads, the rising power in North Africa, took over most of
       <i>
        Al-Andalus
       </i>
       . They would be decisively defeated, however, at the
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Las_Navas_de_Tolosa" title="Battle of Las Navas de Tolosa">
        Battle of Las Navas de Tolosa
       </a>
       (1212) by a Christian coalition, losing almost all the remaining lands of
       <i>
        Al-Andalus
       </i>
       in the following decades. By 1252 only the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Granada" title="Kingdom of Granada">
        Kingdom of Granada
       </a>
       remained as a sovereign Muslim state in the Iberian peninsula.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Granada_War_and_the_end_of_Muslim_rule_in_Iberia">
        Granada War and the end of Muslim rule in Iberia
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Reconquista&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Granada War and the end of Muslim rule in Iberia">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main articles:
       <a href="/wiki/Granada_War" title="Granada War">
        Granada War
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Granada_(1491)" title="Treaty of Granada (1491)">
        Treaty of Granada (1491)
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:La_Rendici%C3%B3n_de_Granada_-_Pradilla.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="5210" data-file-width="8133" height="141" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/La_Rendici%C3%B3n_de_Granada_-_Pradilla.jpg/220px-La_Rendici%C3%B3n_de_Granada_-_Pradilla.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/La_Rendici%C3%B3n_de_Granada_-_Pradilla.jpg/330px-La_Rendici%C3%B3n_de_Granada_-_Pradilla.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/La_Rendici%C3%B3n_de_Granada_-_Pradilla.jpg/440px-La_Rendici%C3%B3n_de_Granada_-_Pradilla.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:La_Rendici%C3%B3n_de_Granada_-_Pradilla.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <i>
          The Surrender of Granada
         </i>
         by
         <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Pradilla_Ortiz" title="Francisco Pradilla Ortiz">
          Francisco Pradilla Ortiz
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Monarchs" title="Catholic Monarchs">
        Ferdinand and Isabella
       </a>
       completed the
       <i>
        Reconquista
       </i>
       with a war against the
       <a href="/wiki/Emirate_of_Granada" title="Emirate of Granada">
        Emirate of Granada
       </a>
       that started in 1482 and ended with Granada's surrender on January 2, 1492. The Moors in Castile previously numbered "half a million within the realm." By 1492 some 100,000 had died or been enslaved, 200,000 had emigrated, and 200,000 remained in Castile. Many of the Muslim elite, including Granada's former Emir Muhammad XII, who had been given the area of the
       <a href="/wiki/Alpujarras" title="Alpujarras">
        Alpujarras
       </a>
       mountains as a principality, found life under Christian rule intolerable and emigrated to
       <a href="/wiki/Tlemcen" title="Tlemcen">
        Tlemcen
       </a>
       in North Africa.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">
        <a href="#cite_note-34">
         [33]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Conversions_and_expulsions">
        Conversions and expulsions
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Reconquista&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Conversions and expulsions">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main articles:
       <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Granada_(1491)" title="Treaty of Granada (1491)">
        Treaty of Granada (1491)
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alhambra_decree" title="Alhambra decree">
        Alhambra decree
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Expulsion_of_the_Moriscos" title="Expulsion of the Moriscos">
        Expulsion of the Moriscos
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Higueruela.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2377" data-file-width="2135" height="245" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Higueruela.jpg/220px-Higueruela.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Higueruela.jpg/330px-Higueruela.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Higueruela.jpg/440px-Higueruela.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Higueruela.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Forces of
         <a href="/wiki/Muhammed_IX,_Sultan_of_Granada" title="Muhammed IX, Sultan of Granada">
          Muhammed IX
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Nasrid_dynasty" title="Nasrid dynasty">
          Nasrid
         </a>
         Sultan of
         <a href="/wiki/Granada" title="Granada">
          Granada
         </a>
         , at the
         <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_La_Higueruela" title="Battle of La Higueruela">
          Battle of La Higueruela
         </a>
         , 1431
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       During the Islamic administration, Christians and Jews were allowed to retain their religions by paying a
       <a href="/wiki/Jizya" title="Jizya">
        tax
       </a>
       <i>
        (jizya)
       </i>
       . Penalty for not paying it was imprisonment.
      </p>
      <p>
       The new Christian hierarchy demanded heavy taxes from non-Christians and gave them rights, such as in the
       <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Granada_(1491)" title="Treaty of Granada (1491)">
        Treaty of Granada (1491)
       </a>
       only for Moors in recently Islamic Granada. On July 30, 1492, all the Jewish community — some 200,000 people — were forcibly expelled.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">
        <a href="#cite_note-35">
         [34]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The very next year the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alhambra_decree" title="Alhambra decree">
        Alhambra decree
       </a>
       under
       <a href="/wiki/Archbishop" title="Archbishop">
        Archbishop
       </a>
       Hernando de Talavera (1492) dismissed the Treaty of Granada and now the Muslim population of Granada was forced to convert or be expelled. In 1502, Queen Isabella I declared conversion to Catholicism compulsory within the Kingdom of Castile. King
       <a href="/wiki/Charles_V,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Charles V, Holy Roman Emperor">
        Charles V
       </a>
       did the same to Moors in the Kingdom of Aragon in 1526, forcing conversions of its Muslim population during the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Revolt_of_the_Germanies" title="Revolt of the Germanies">
        Revolt of the Germanies
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tofiño_36-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Tofiño-36">
         [35]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Many local officials took advantage of the situation to seize property.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Spanish_Inquisition">
        Spanish Inquisition
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Reconquista&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Spanish Inquisition">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Inquisition" title="Spanish Inquisition">
        Spanish Inquisition
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Most of the descendants of those Muslims who submitted to conversion to Christianity rather than exile during the early periods of the Spanish and Portuguese Inquisition, the Moriscos, were later
       <a href="/wiki/Expulsion_of_the_Moriscos" title="Expulsion of the Moriscos">
        expelled from Spain
       </a>
       after serious social upheaval, when the Inquisition was at its height. The expulsions were carried out more severely in eastern Spain (Valencia and Aragon) due to local animosity towards Muslims and Moriscos where they were seen as economic rivals by local workers who saw them as cheap labor undermining their bargaining position with the landlords. Exactions imposed on the Moriscos paved the way to a major
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Morisco_revolt" title="Morisco revolt">
        Morisco revolt
       </a>
       happening in 1568, with the final
       <a href="/wiki/Expulsion_of_the_Moriscos" title="Expulsion of the Moriscos">
        expulsion of the Moriscos
       </a>
       from
       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Castile" title="Kingdom of Castile">
        Castile
       </a>
       taking place in 1609; they were driven from
       <a href="/wiki/Aragon" title="Aragon">
        Aragon
       </a>
       at about the same time.
      </p>
      <p>
       Making things more complex were the many former Muslims and Jews known as
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Morisco" title="Morisco">
         Moriscos
        </a>
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Marrano" title="Marrano">
         Marranos
        </a>
       </i>
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Converso" title="Converso">
         Conversos
        </a>
       </i>
       who shared ancestors in common with many Christians, especially among the aristocracy, causing much concern over loyalty and attempts by the aristocracy to hide their non-Christian ancestry. Those that the
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Inquisition" title="Spanish Inquisition">
        Spanish Inquisition
       </a>
       found to be secretly practicing Islam or Judaism were executed, imprisoned or expelled. Nevertheless, all those deemed to be "New Christians" were perpetually suspected of various
       <a href="/wiki/Treason" title="Treason">
        crimes against the Spanish state
       </a>
       including continued practice of Islam or Judaism.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Classifications_and_later_consequences">
        Classifications and later consequences
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Reconquista&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Classifications and later consequences">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pedro_Berruguete_Saint_Dominic_Presiding_over_an_Auto-da-fe_1495.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3051" data-file-width="1892" height="355" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Pedro_Berruguete_Saint_Dominic_Presiding_over_an_Auto-da-fe_1495.jpg/220px-Pedro_Berruguete_Saint_Dominic_Presiding_over_an_Auto-da-fe_1495.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Pedro_Berruguete_Saint_Dominic_Presiding_over_an_Auto-da-fe_1495.jpg/330px-Pedro_Berruguete_Saint_Dominic_Presiding_over_an_Auto-da-fe_1495.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Pedro_Berruguete_Saint_Dominic_Presiding_over_an_Auto-da-fe_1495.jpg/440px-Pedro_Berruguete_Saint_Dominic_Presiding_over_an_Auto-da-fe_1495.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pedro_Berruguete_Saint_Dominic_Presiding_over_an_Auto-da-fe_1495.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Saint_Dominic" title="Saint Dominic">
          Saint Dominic
         </a>
         presiding over an
         <i>
          auto-da-fé
         </i>
         , by
         <a href="/wiki/Pedro_Berruguete" title="Pedro Berruguete">
          Pedro Berruguete
         </a>
         (around 1495)
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Prado_37-0">
          <a href="#cite_note-Prado-37">
           [36]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The many advances and retreats created several social types:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        The
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Muladi" title="Muladi">
          Muladi
         </a>
        </i>
        : Christians under Islamic rule who converted to Islam after the arrival of the Moors.
       </li>
       <li>
        The
        <i>
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mozarab" title="Mozarab">
          Mozarabs
         </a>
        </i>
        : Christians in Muslim-held lands. Some of them migrated to the north of the peninsula in times of persecution bringing elements of the styles, food and agricultural practices learned from the Moors, while they continued practicing their Christianity with older forms of Catholic worship and their own versions of the
        <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">
         Latin
        </a>
        language.
       </li>
       <li>
        "
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_Christians" title="New Christians">
         New Christians
        </a>
        ", Jews converting to Christianity called
        <i>
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Conversos" title="Conversos">
          conversos
         </a>
        </i>
        , or pejoratively
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Marrano" title="Marrano">
          Marranos
         </a>
        </i>
        . Jews converted to Christianity voluntarily or through force. Some were
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Crypto-Jews" title="Crypto-Jews">
         Crypto-Jews
        </a>
        who continued practicing
        <a href="/wiki/Judaism" title="Judaism">
         Judaism
        </a>
        secretly. All remaining Jews were expelled from Spain as a consequence of the 1492
        <a href="/wiki/Alhambra_Decree" title="Alhambra Decree">
         Alhambra Decree
        </a>
        , and from Portugal in 1497.
        <i>
         Converso
        </i>
        Jews were subject to the
        <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Inquisition" title="Spanish Inquisition">
         Spanish
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Inquisition" title="Portuguese Inquisition">
         Portuguese Inquisitions
        </a>
        , established to enforce Christian faith and practice, which often resulted in secret investigations and public punishments of
        <i>
         conversos
        </i>
        in
        <a href="/wiki/Auto-da-f%C3%A9" title="Auto-da-fé">
         autos-de-fé
        </a>
        ("acts of faith").
       </li>
       <li>
        The
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Mud%C3%A9jar" title="Mudéjar">
          Mudéjar
         </a>
        </i>
        : Muslims in Christian-held lands.
       </li>
       <li>
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Morisco" title="Morisco">
          Moriscos
         </a>
        </i>
        : Muslim
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Converso" title="Converso">
          conversos
         </a>
        </i>
        . Muslims who were forced to convert to Catholicism. A significant number were Crypto-Muslims who continued practicing Islam secretly. They ranged from successful skilled artisans, valued and protected in Aragon, to impoverished peasants in Castile. After the
        <a href="/wiki/Alhambra_Decree" title="Alhambra Decree">
         Alhambra Decree
        </a>
        the entire Islamic population was forced to convert or leave, and at the beginning of the seventeenth century a significant number were expelled in the
        <a href="/wiki/Expulsion_of_the_Moriscos" title="Expulsion of the Moriscos">
         Expulsion of the Moriscos
        </a>
        .
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Legacy">
        Legacy
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Reconquista&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Legacy">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_Spain" title="History of Spain">
        History of Spain
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_Portugal" title="History of Portugal">
        History of Portugal
       </a>
       , and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Portugal_in_the_period_of_discoveries" title="Portugal in the period of discoveries">
        Portugal in the period of discoveries
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Real, legendary, and fictional episodes from the
       <i>
        Reconquista
       </i>
       are the subject of much of medieval
       <a href="/wiki/Galician-Portuguese" title="Galician-Portuguese">
        Galician-Portuguese
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_literature" title="Spanish literature">
        Spanish
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Catalan_literature" title="Catalan literature">
        Catalan literature
       </a>
       such as the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Cantar_de_gesta" title="Cantar de gesta">
         cantar de gesta
        </a>
       </i>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Some noble
       <a href="/wiki/Genealogy" title="Genealogy">
        genealogies
       </a>
       show the close relations (although not very numerous) between Muslims and Christians. For example,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Al-Mansur_Ibn_Abi_Aamir" title="Al-Mansur Ibn Abi Aamir">
        Al-Mansur Ibn Abi Aamir
       </a>
       , whose rule is considered to have marked the peak of power for Moorish
       <i>
        Al-Andalus
       </i>
       Iberia, married Abda, daughter of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sancho_II_of_Navarra" title="Sancho II of Navarra">
        Sancho Garcés II
       </a>
       of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Navarra" title="Navarra">
        Navarra
       </a>
       , who bore him a son, named Abd al-Rahman and commonly known in pejorative sense as
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sanchuelo" title="Sanchuelo">
        Sanchuelo
       </a>
       (
       <i>
        Little Sancho
       </i>
       ; in Arabic:
       <i>
        Shanjoul
       </i>
       ).
      </p>
      <p>
       After his father's death, Sanchuelo/Abd al-Rahman, as a son of a Christian princess, was a strong contender to take over the ultimate power in Muslim al-Andalus. A hundred years later, King
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alfonso_VI_of_Castile" title="Alfonso VI of Castile">
        Alfonso VI of Castile
       </a>
       , considered among the greatest of the Medieval Spanish kings, designated as his heir his son (also a Sancho) by the refugee
       <a href="/wiki/Muslim" title="Muslim">
        Muslim
       </a>
       princess
       <a href="/wiki/Zaida_of_Seville" title="Zaida of Seville">
        Zaida of Seville
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <i>
        Reconquista
       </i>
       was a war with long periods of respite between the adversaries, partly for pragmatic reasons and also due to infighting among the Christian kingdoms of the North spanning over seven centuries. Some populations practiced Islam or Christianity as their own religion during these centuries, so the identity of contenders changed over time.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Festivals_in_modern_Spain">
        Festivals in modern Spain
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Reconquista&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Festivals in modern Spain">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Currently, the festivals of
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Moros_y_cristianos" title="Moros y cristianos">
         moros y cristianos
        </a>
       </i>
       (Castilian),
       <i>
        moros i cristians
       </i>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Catalan_language" title="Catalan language">
        Catalan
       </a>
       ),
       <i>
        mouros e cristãos
       </i>
       (Portuguese) and
       <i>
        mouros e cristiáns
       </i>
       (Galician), these meaning "Moors and Christians", recreate the fights as colorful parades with elaborate garments and lots of fireworks, especially on the central and southern towns of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Land_of_Valencia" title="Land of Valencia">
        Land of Valencia
       </a>
       , like
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alcoi" title="Alcoi">
        Alcoi
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Ontinyent" title="Ontinyent">
        Ontinyent
       </a>
       or
       <a href="/wiki/Villena" title="Villena">
        Villena
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Persistent_effects">
        Persistent effects
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Reconquista&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Persistent effects">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       A 2016 study found that the manner of the Reconquest has persistent effects on the Spanish economy to this day.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_38-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-:0-38">
         [37]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The authors show how territory quickly re-taken during the Reconquest was given to nobility, whereas territory slowly re-taken was more equally distributed and settled.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_38-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-:0-38">
         [37]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Lands dominated by nobility have worse long-term development outcomes and greater inequality.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_38-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-:0-38">
         [37]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Timeline_of_major_dates">
        Timeline of major dates
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Reconquista&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Timeline of major dates">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Timeline_of_the_Muslim_presence_in_the_Iberian_peninsula" title="Timeline of the Muslim presence in the Iberian peninsula">
        Timeline of the Muslim presence in the Iberian peninsula
       </a>
      </div>
      <ul>
       <li>
        711: The invasion of Christian Visigothic-ruled Iberia by Islamic Arab-Berber armies of the Umayyad Caliphate begins.
       </li>
       <li>
        717: First Umayyad foray
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Islamic_invasion_of_Gaul" title="Islamic invasion of Gaul">
         over the Pyrenees into Visigothic Gaul
        </a>
        .
       </li>
       <li>
        719:
        <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">
         Islamic
        </a>
        <a href="/wiki/Umayyad_Caliphate" title="Umayyad Caliphate">
         Umayyad
        </a>
        rule in Iberia at its widest, covering almost all of the Iberian Peninsula and across the Pyrenees in Narbonne.
       </li>
       <li>
        718 or 722:
        <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Covadonga" title="Battle of Covadonga">
         Battle of Covadonga
        </a>
        in the north-west of Iberia, establishing a Christian Kingdom in Asturias.
       </li>
       <li>
        739 Berber garrison driven from Galicia.
        <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
         [
         <i>
          <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
           <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2014)">
            citation needed
           </span>
          </a>
         </i>
         ]
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        742: Berber garrisons give up their positions north of the
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Duero_River" title="Duero River">
         Duero River
        </a>
        to join the
        <a href="/wiki/Berber_Revolt" title="Berber Revolt">
         Berber rebellion
        </a>
        .
       </li>
       <li>
        759:
        <a href="/wiki/Pepin_the_Short" title="Pepin the Short">
         Pepin the Short
        </a>
        conquers the last Muslim strongholds in present-day France.
       </li>
       <li>
        801: The Carolingians led by
        <a href="/wiki/Louis_the_Pious" title="Louis the Pious">
         Louis the Pious
        </a>
        conquer
        <a href="/wiki/Barcelona" title="Barcelona">
         Barcelona
        </a>
        , sack
        <a href="/wiki/Lleida" title="Lleida">
         Lleida
        </a>
        , and establish the
        <a href="/wiki/Marca_Hispanica" title="Marca Hispanica">
         Spanish March
        </a>
        .
       </li>
       <li>
        809: The Carolingians fail to take and hold
        <a href="/wiki/Tarragona" title="Tarragona">
         Tarragona
        </a>
        and Tortosa, retreating to their Ebro marches.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Collins1990_39-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-Collins1990-39">
          [38]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
         :
         <span>
          124
         </span>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        868: Conquest of the city of
        <a href="/wiki/Porto" title="Porto">
         Porto
        </a>
        , leading to the establishment of the
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/County_of_Portucale" title="County of Portucale">
         County of Portucale
        </a>
        (Latin for later Portugal).
       </li>
       <li>
        871: Capture of
        <a href="/wiki/Coimbra" title="Coimbra">
         Coimbra
        </a>
        by the Asturians,
        <a href="/wiki/County_of_Coimbra" title="County of Coimbra">
         County of Coimbra
        </a>
        established.
       </li>
       <li>
        914:
        <a href="/wiki/Al-Andalus" title="Al-Andalus">
         Muslims
        </a>
        briefly retake Barcelona.
       </li>
       <li>
        929
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Abd_al-Rahman_III" title="Abd al-Rahman III">
         Abd al-Rahman III
        </a>
        declares caliphate in
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/C%C3%B3rdoba,_Andalusia" title="Córdoba, Andalusia">
         Córdoba
        </a>
        , taking the title of "commander of the faithful" (caliph).
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">
         <a href="#cite_note-40">
          [39]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        1085: Landmark conquest of
        <a href="/wiki/Toledo,_Spain" title="Toledo, Spain">
         Toledo
        </a>
        by Castilian forces. Over half of Iberia conquered by Christian-ruled kingdoms.
       </li>
       <li>
        1086:
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Almoravid" title="Almoravid">
         Almoravid
        </a>
        defeated Castilian army and halted its advance at
        <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Sagrajas" title="Battle of Sagrajas">
         Battle of Sagrajas
        </a>
        .
       </li>
       <li>
        1097:
        <a href="/wiki/First_Crusade" title="First Crusade">
         First Crusade
        </a>
        ; two-thirds of the Iberian peninsula conquered by Christian-ruled kingdoms.
       </li>
       <li>
        1118: Navarro-Aragonese troops capture the Muslim strongholds of
        <a href="/wiki/Tudela,_Navarre" title="Tudela, Navarre">
         Tudela
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/Zaragoza" title="Zaragoza">
         Zaragoza
        </a>
        .
       </li>
       <li>
        1147:
        <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Lisbon" title="Siege of Lisbon">
         Siege of Lisbon
        </a>
        , where Second Crusade and the Kingdom of Portugal defeat the
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Almoravids" title="Almoravids">
         Almoravids
        </a>
        .
       </li>
       <li>
        1148:
        <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Tortosa_(1148)" title="Siege of Tortosa (1148)">
         Siege of Tortosa
        </a>
        , part of the Second Crusade
       </li>
       <li>
        1195: The
        <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Alarcos" title="Battle of Alarcos">
         Battle of Alarcos
        </a>
        establishes
        <a href="/wiki/Almohad_Caliphate" title="Almohad Caliphate">
         Almohad
        </a>
        authority in the south of the Iberia.
       </li>
       <li>
        1212: The key battle of
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Navas_de_Tolosa" title="Navas de Tolosa">
         Navas de Tolosa
        </a>
        heralds the steady political decline of the Iberian Muslim kingdoms.
       </li>
       <li>
        1236:
        <a href="/wiki/C%C3%A1diz" title="Cádiz">
         Cádiz
        </a>
        and the former capital of the caliphate
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/C%C3%B3rdoba,_Andalusia" title="Córdoba, Andalusia">
         Córdoba
        </a>
        are conquered by Castilian forces.
       </li>
       <li>
        1248: Christian armies under
        <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_III_of_Castile" title="Ferdinand III of Castile">
         Ferdinand III of Castile
        </a>
        take
        <a href="/wiki/Seville" title="Seville">
         Seville
        </a>
        after 16 months of siege.
       </li>
       <li>
        1249: King
        <a href="/wiki/Afonso_III_of_Portugal" title="Afonso III of Portugal">
         Afonso III of Portugal
        </a>
        takes
        <a href="/wiki/Faro,_Portugal" title="Faro, Portugal">
         Faro
        </a>
        (in the Algarve), ending the Portuguese
        <i>
         Reconquista
        </i>
        in 1249.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">
         <a href="#cite_note-41">
          [40]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        1249: The Emirate of Granada is now the only Islamic state in Iberia.
       </li>
       <li>
        14th and 15th centuries: Marinid Muslims seize control of some towns on the southern coast but are soon driven out, leaving only a few isolated towns in the south of Granada still controlled by the Moors.
       </li>
       <li>
        1492: Following the
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Granada" title="Treaty of Granada">
         Treaty of Granada
        </a>
        (25 November 1491), the Moors surrender the city, completing the military phase of the
        <i>
         Reconquista
        </i>
        .
       </li>
       <li>
        1492:
        <a href="/wiki/Alhambra_Decree" title="Alhambra Decree">
         Alhambra Decree
        </a>
        issued by the
        <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Monarchs" title="Catholic Monarchs">
         Catholic Monarchs
        </a>
        31 March expelling Jews from Spain
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">
         <a href="#cite_note-42">
          [41]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
      </ul>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">
        Notes
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Reconquista&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Notes">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: lower-alpha;">
       <div class="mw-references-wrap">
        <ol class="references">
         <li id="cite_note-1">
          <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
           <b>
            <a href="#cite_ref-1">
             ^
            </a>
           </b>
          </span>
          <span class="reference-text">
           While spelled largely the same, the pronunciation differs among the different Iberian languages, mostly in accordance with the sound structures of the respective languages. The pronunciations are as
          </span>
          <ul>
           <li>
            <span class="reference-text">
             <small>
              Galician:
             </small>
             <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
              <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Galician" title="Help:IPA/Galician">
               [rekoŋˈkista]
              </a>
             </span>
            </span>
           </li>
           <li>
            <small>
             Asturian:
            </small>
            <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
             <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Astur-Leonese" title="Help:IPA/Astur-Leonese">
              [rekoŋˈkista]
             </a>
            </span>
           </li>
           <li>
            <small>
             Portuguese:
            </small>
            <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
             <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Portuguese" title="Help:IPA/Portuguese">
              [ʁəcɔŋˈkiʃtɐ]
             </a>
            </span>
           </li>
           <li>
            <small>
             Catalan:
            </small>
            <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
             <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Catalan" title="Help:IPA/Catalan">
              [rəkuŋˈkestə]
             </a>
            </span>
            <small>
             or
            </small>
            <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
             <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Catalan" title="Help:IPA/Catalan">
              [rekoŋˈkesta]
             </a>
            </span>
            , spelled
            <i>
             Reconquesta
            </i>
            . Colloquially also known and spelled as
            <i>
             Reconquista
            </i>
            (
            <small>
             pron.
            </small>
            <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
             <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Catalan" title="Help:IPA/Catalan">
              [rəkuŋˈkistə]
             </a>
            </span>
            <small>
             or
            </small>
            <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
             <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Catalan" title="Help:IPA/Catalan">
              [rekoŋˈkista]
             </a>
            </span>
            ).
           </li>
           <li>
            <small>
             Basque:
            </small>
            <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
             <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Basque" title="Help:IPA/Basque">
              [erekoŋkis̺ta]
             </a>
            </span>
            , spelled
            <i>
             Errekonkista
            </i>
           </li>
          </ul>
         </li>
        </ol>
       </div>
      </div>

           </b>
